Towards sequencing the papaya sex chromosomes, two bacterial artificial chromosome (BAC) libraries were constructed from papaya male and female genomic DNA. The female BAC library was constructed using restriction enzyme<jats:italic>Bst</jats:italic>Y I and consists of 36,864 clones with an average insert size of 104\u2009kb, providing 10.3x genome equivalents. The male BAC library was constructed using restriction enzyme<jats:italic>Eco</jats:italic>R I and consists of 55,296 clones with an average insert size of 101\u2009kb, providing 15.0x genome equivalents. The male BAC library was used in constructing the physical map of the male-specific region of the male Y chromosome (MSY) and in filling gaps and extending the physical map of the hermaphrodite-specific region of the Y<jats:sup>h</jats:sup>chromosome (HSY) and the X chromosome physical map. The female BAC library was used to extend the X physical map gap. The MSY, HSY, and X physical maps offer a unique opportunity to study chromosomal rearrangements, Y chromosome degeneration, and dosage compensation of the papaya nascent sex chromosomes.</jats:p>",
